Economic Reforms Quiz

Question 1easy

India is classified as a:

  1. Mixed economy — combines elements of market economy (private sector, price mechanism) and planned economy (government intervention, public sector)
  2. Pure socialist economy
  3. Pure capitalist economy
  4. Closed economy
Show answer

Answer: Mixed economy — combines elements of market economy (private sector, price mechanism) and planned economy (government intervention, public sector)

India's mixed economy (as in the Constitution's Directive Principles): public sector controls strategic industries (defense, rail, atomic energy), while private sector operates in most areas. Since 1991 reforms, India has moved significantly toward market economy with reduced government control.

Question 2medium

Pension reforms in India were initiated with the establishment of:

  1. PFRDA (Pension Fund Regulatory and Development Authority, 2003) — regulates NPS, APY, and other pension schemes; statutory status 2014 under PFRDA Act
  2. LIC
  3. RBI
  4. SEBI
Show answer

Answer: PFRDA (Pension Fund Regulatory and Development Authority, 2003) — regulates NPS, APY, and other pension schemes; statutory status 2014 under PFRDA Act

PFRDA (Pension Fund Regulatory and Development Authority): interim PFRDA set up 2003 to manage NPS rollout for new central government employees. PFRDA Act 2013 (in force 2014) gave it statutory status. Regulates: NPS (National Pension System — for government and private sector), APY (Atal Pension Yojana — for unorganized sector). Fund managers: SBI, LIC, HDFC, ICICI Prudential, Kotak, UTI, Aditya Birla.

Question 3easy

Privatization of Air India was completed in:

  1. January 2022 — Tata Sons (through Talace Pvt Ltd) acquired Air India for Rs 18,000 crore; ending government ownership since 1953 nationalization; Air India's homecoming to Tatas (original founder JRD Tata)
  2. 2019
  3. 2015
  4. 2010
Show answer

Answer: January 2022 — Tata Sons (through Talace Pvt Ltd) acquired Air India for Rs 18,000 crore; ending government ownership since 1953 nationalization; Air India's homecoming to Tatas (original founder JRD Tata)

Air India disinvestment: launched 2020, completed January 27, 2022. Tata Sons won the bid with enterprise value of Rs 18,000 crore (Rs 2,700 crore cash + Rs 15,300 crore debt assumption). Air India was founded by J.R.D. Tata (1932 as Tata Airlines) → nationalized 1953 → returned to Tatas after 69 years. Tata also owns Vistara, Air Asia India (merged into Air India).

Question 4medium

The 'Big Bang' approach to economic reforms (as opposed to 'gradualism') involves:

  1. Slow, phased implementation of reforms
  2. Rapid, simultaneous implementation of multiple major reforms
  3. Only monetary reforms
  4. Only trade reforms
Show answer

Answer: Rapid, simultaneous implementation of multiple major reforms

Big Bang reforms: comprehensive, rapid liberalization across sectors simultaneously (Poland 1990, Russia early 1990s). Contrasts with China's and India's gradual approach. India's 1991 reforms were bold but not full 'big bang.'

Question 5hard

The National Monetization Pipeline (NMP) was announced by:

  1. FM Nirmala Sitharaman in August 2021 — plan to monetize Rs 6 lakh crore of brownfield government infrastructure assets (roads, railways, power lines, gas pipelines, airports) over 4 years
  2. PM Modi in 2019
  3. Planning Commission in 2015
  4. NITI Aayog in 2016
Show answer

Answer: FM Nirmala Sitharaman in August 2021 — plan to monetize Rs 6 lakh crore of brownfield government infrastructure assets (roads, railways, power lines, gas pipelines, airports) over 4 years

NMP (National Monetization Pipeline, 2021-2025): aims to raise Rs 6 lakh crore by transferring operation of existing government assets (brownfield) to private sector for a fixed period (not selling assets). Assets: NHAI roads, railway stations/freight terminals, power lines (PGCIL), gas pipelines (GAIL), airports (AAI), ports. Asset monetization ≠ privatization.

Question 6easy

The Model Agricultural Produce Marketing Committee (APMC) Act, 2003, introduced by the central government, primarily aimed to:

  1. Nationalize all agricultural markets
  2. Allow private sector participation in agricultural marketing
  3. Abolish minimum support prices for all crops
  4. Impose quantitative restrictions on agricultural exports
Show answer

Answer: Allow private sector participation in agricultural marketing

The Model APMC Act 2003 sought to allow private markets, direct purchases, and contract farming, breaking the monopoly of state APMCs.

Question 7easy

Which of the following is NOT a quantitative tool of monetary policy used by the Reserve Bank of India?

  1. Bank Rate
  2. Open Market Operations
  3. Credit Authorization Scheme
  4. Marginal Standing Facility
Show answer

Answer: Credit Authorization Scheme

Credit Authorization Scheme is a qualitative (selective) credit control tool, whereas Bank Rate, OMO, and MSF are quantitative instruments.

Question 8easy

The difference between the fiscal deficit and the interest payments of the government is known as:

  1. Revenue deficit
  2. Primary deficit
  3. Capital deficit
  4. Budgetary deficit
Show answer

Answer: Primary deficit

Primary deficit equals fiscal deficit minus interest payments, indicating current year's borrowing net of past debt obligations.

Question 9easy

In India, the headline inflation rate that serves as the nominal anchor for monetary policy is currently measured by:

  1. Wholesale Price Index (WPI)
  2. Consumer Price Index (CPI)
  3. GDP Deflator
  4. Producer Price Index (PPI)
Show answer

Answer: Consumer Price Index (CPI)

Since 2014, the RBI uses CPI (Combined) as the inflation anchor under flexible inflation targeting, replacing WPI.

Question 10easy

A persistent surplus in the current account of India's balance of payments indicates that:

  1. The country is a net borrower from the rest of the world
  2. Exports of goods, services, and transfers exceed imports
  3. The country has a deficit in the capital account
  4. The rupee is depreciating against the dollar
Show answer

Answer: Exports of goods, services, and transfers exceed imports

A current account surplus means exports of goods, services, and net transfers are greater than imports of the same.

Question 11easy

Consider the following effects of rupee depreciation against the US dollar: 1. Imports become costlier 2. Exports become more competitive 3. Foreign currency-denominated debt becomes cheaper to repay 4. Inflation may rise due to imported inflation. Which of the above are correct?

  1. 1 and 2 only
  2. 1, 2, and 4 only
  3. 1, 2, and 3 only
  4. 1, 2, 3, and 4
Show answer

Answer: 1, 2, and 4 only

Depreciation makes imports costlier, boosts export competitiveness, and triggers imported inflation; however, foreign debt becomes costlier, not cheaper.

Question 12easy

'Sterilized intervention' by a central bank in the foreign exchange market refers to:

  1. Buying foreign exchange without affecting domestic money supply
  2. Selling foreign exchange to prevent currency appreciation
  3. Offsetting the monetary impact of forex operations on domestic money supply
  4. Restricting cross-border capital flows
Show answer

Answer: Offsetting the monetary impact of forex operations on domestic money supply

Sterilization means the central bank neutralizes the impact of forex inflows/outflows on domestic money supply through offsetting open market operations.

Question 13easy

The New Industrial Policy of 1991, which marked the beginning of economic reforms in India, was based on which of the following approaches?

  1. Import substitution and tight licensing
  2. Liberalization, Privatization, and Globalization
  3. Complete nationalization of industries
  4. Centrally planned economy
Show answer

Answer: Liberalization, Privatization, and Globalization

The 1991 reforms under PM Narasimha Rao and FM Manmohan Singh adopted the LPG framework to shift from a controlled to a market-oriented economy.

Question 14easy

The strategic sale of public sector enterprises in India, as opposed to minority disinvestment, aims to:

  1. Retain government control while raising revenue
  2. Transfer management control to private entities and raise substantial revenue
  3. Issue employee stock options only
  4. Convert public debt into equity
Show answer

Answer: Transfer management control to private entities and raise substantial revenue

Strategic disinvestment involves selling a substantial stake (often over 50%), resulting in transfer of management control to the private buyer.

Question 15easy

Despite high economic growth after the 1991 economic reforms, the gap between the rich and poor in India widened significantly. This phenomenon is referred to as:

  1. Trickle-down effect
  2. Inclusive growth
  3. Growth paradox or rising inequality
  4. Vicious circle of poverty
Show answer

Answer: Growth paradox or rising inequality

Post-1991 India experienced a 'growth paradox' where high GDP growth did not translate proportionally into poverty reduction, leading to widening inequality.

Question 16easy

In the context of India's 1991 Economic Reforms, which of the following best describes the primary objective of 'Devaluation' of the Rupee?

  1. To increase the cost of imports to discourage luxury consumption
  2. To make Indian exports more competitive in the global market
  3. To reduce the domestic inflation rate by limiting imports
  4. To increase the value of foreign exchange reserves through direct purchase
Show answer

Answer: To make Indian exports more competitive in the global market

Devaluation makes domestic goods cheaper for foreign buyers, thereby boosting exports and improving the current account balance.

Question 17easy

Which of the following is a direct consequence of 'Sterilized Intervention' conducted by the Reserve Bank of India (RBI)?

  1. A decrease in the overall money supply to curb inflation
  2. The neutralization of the impact of foreign exchange inflows on domestic liquidity
  3. An automatic increase in the value of the Rupee against the Dollar
  4. A mandatory increase in the Cash Reserve Ratio for commercial banks
Show answer

Answer: The neutralization of the impact of foreign exchange inflows on domestic liquidity

Sterilization involves offsetting the increase in money supply caused by forex purchases by selling government securities.

Question 18easy

Regarding the 'Fiscal Responsibility and Budget Management (FRBM) Act', what is the primary conceptual goal of targeting a specific fiscal deficit limit?

  1. To ensure that the government spends more on capital assets than revenue expenditure
  2. To eliminate the need for external borrowing from the IMF
  3. To ensure long-term macroeconomic stability by limiting government borrowing
  4. To mandate a balanced budget where expenditure exactly equals revenue
Show answer

Answer: To ensure long-term macroeconomic stability by limiting government borrowing

The FRBM Act aims to institutionalize financial discipline to ensure sustainability of public debt and stability.

Question 19easy

If the RBI decides to increase the 'Weighted Average Call Rate' through open market operations, what is the most likely impact on the economy?

  1. Cost of short-term borrowing for banks increases, potentially raising lending rates
  2. The Rupee will immediately depreciate against the US Dollar
  3. Foreign Portfolio Investment (FPI) will decrease due to higher costs
  4. The government's fiscal deficit will automatically widen
Show answer

Answer: Cost of short-term borrowing for banks increases, potentially raising lending rates

Higher call rates increase the cost of inter-bank borrowing, which typically trickles down to higher lending rates for consumers.

Question 20easy

Which of the following statements correctly describes the impact of a 'depreciating Rupee' on India's Balance of Payments?

  1. It leads to a decrease in the value of remittances sent by NRIs
  2. It generally makes imports cheaper, improving the trade balance
  3. It may improve the trade balance by making exports cheaper and imports costlier
  4. It leads to an automatic decrease in the Capital Account deficit
Show answer

Answer: It may improve the trade balance by making exports cheaper and imports costlier

Depreciation makes exports more attractive to foreigners and imports more expensive for locals, potentially reducing the trade deficit.

Question 21easy

In the context of agricultural reforms, 'Contract Farming' is primarily intended to address which of the following systemic issues?

  1. The lack of land ownership among marginal farmers
  2. Price volatility and lack of assured markets for farmers
  3. The over-reliance on chemical fertilizers and pesticides
  4. The inefficiency of the irrigation systems in rain-fed areas
Show answer

Answer: Price volatility and lack of assured markets for farmers

Contract farming provides price certainty and market access by linking farmers directly with buyers before sowing.

Question 22easy

Which of the following is a characteristic of 'Inflation Targeting' as adopted by the Monetary Policy Committee (MPC) of India?

  1. Fixing the exchange rate of the Rupee against a basket of currencies
  2. Using the Repo Rate as the primary tool to keep inflation within a specified range
  3. Setting a fixed price for essential commodities to prevent price hikes
  4. Prioritizing GDP growth over price stability during economic downturns
Show answer

Answer: Using the Repo Rate as the primary tool to keep inflation within a specified range

Inflation targeting focuses on maintaining CPI inflation within a target band using the repo rate as the main instrument.

Question 23easy

What is the conceptual difference between 'Primary Deficit' and 'Fiscal Deficit'?

  1. Primary deficit excludes the interest payments on previous borrowings
  2. Fiscal deficit excludes the revenue deficit from the total
  3. Primary deficit includes only the external debt payments
  4. Fiscal deficit represents only the borrowing from the RBI
Show answer

Answer: Primary deficit excludes the interest payments on previous borrowings

Primary Deficit = Fiscal Deficit minus Interest Payments, showing the borrowing needs excluding past debt obligations.

Question 24easy

Which of the following best explains the 'Crowding Out' effect in the context of government borrowing?

  1. Increased government spending leading to a surge in private investment
  2. High government borrowing increasing interest rates and reducing private investment
  3. Foreign investors exiting the market due to high domestic inflation
  4. The replacement of manual labor by automation in the industrial sector
Show answer

Answer: High government borrowing increasing interest rates and reducing private investment

When government borrows heavily, it competes for limited loanable funds, driving up interest rates and deterring private investment.

Question 25easy

Under the 'Goods and Services Tax (GST)' reform, the 'Input Tax Credit' mechanism is designed to prevent which of the following?

  1. The accumulation of trade deficits with trading partners
  2. The cascading effect of taxes (tax on tax)
  3. The increase in the overall price of luxury goods
  4. The shift from formal to informal economic sectors
Show answer

Answer: The cascading effect of taxes (tax on tax)

Input Tax Credit allows sellers to claim credit for taxes paid on inputs, eliminating the cascading effect of multiple taxes.

Question 26easy

With reference to the 'LPG' reforms introduced in 1991, which of the following best describes the primary objective of 'Liberalization' in the Indian context?

  1. Increasing the share of foreign ownership in all public sector undertakings
  2. Reducing government control over economic activities and removing license raj
  3. Complete elimination of all tariffs on imported capital goods
  4. Shifting the entire economy from a mixed economy to a pure market economy
Show answer

Answer: Reducing government control over economic activities and removing license raj

Liberalization aimed to remove unnecessary bureaucratic controls and the licensing system to encourage private sector growth.

Question 27easy

In the context of monetary policy reforms, what is the primary purpose of 'Sterilized Intervention' by the Reserve Bank of India?

  1. To increase the money supply to combat deflationary pressures
  2. To neutralize the effect of foreign exchange inflows on the domestic money supply
  3. To permanently fix the exchange rate of the Rupee against the US Dollar
  4. To eliminate the need for Open Market Operations
Show answer

Answer: To neutralize the effect of foreign exchange inflows on the domestic money supply

Sterilization prevents excess liquidity from foreign exchange inflows from causing inflation by absorbing funds through bonds.

Question 28easy

Which of the following is a direct consequence of the 'Managed Floating Exchange Rate' system adopted by India?

  1. The Rupee's value is fixed strictly against a basket of currencies
  2. The RBI does not intervene in the forex market at any cost
  3. The exchange rate is determined by market forces but the RBI intervenes to curb volatility
  4. The government decides the exchange rate daily through a fixed decree
Show answer

Answer: The exchange rate is determined by market forces but the RBI intervenes to curb volatility

Under a managed float, market forces determine the rate, but the central bank intervenes to prevent excessive volatility.

Question 29easy

Regarding the reform of the 'Goods and Services Tax' (GST), which of the following statements is correct regarding its impact on the 'cascading effect'?

  1. It increased the cascading effect by adding multiple layers of taxes
  2. It eliminated the tax-on-tax effect by providing Input Tax Credit
  3. It replaced only the direct taxes to simplify the tax structure
  4. It created a dual-taxation system where both VAT and GST are paid on the same product
Show answer

Answer: It eliminated the tax-on-tax effect by providing Input Tax Credit

GST reduced the cascading effect by allowing credit for taxes paid on inputs, ensuring tax is levied only on value addition.

Question 30easy

In the context of fiscal reforms, 'Fiscal Consolidation' primarily refers to which of the following processes?

  1. Increasing the total government expenditure to stimulate demand
  2. The process of reducing the government's fiscal deficit to a sustainable level
  3. Shifting from a progressive tax system to a regressive tax system
  4. Increasing the borrowing from the RBI to fund infrastructure projects
Show answer

Answer: The process of reducing the government's fiscal deficit to a sustainable level

Fiscal consolidation involves reducing the gap between government expenditure and revenue to ensure long-term debt sustainability.

Question 31easy

How does the 'Automatic Route' for Foreign Direct Investment (FDI) differ from the 'Government Route'?

  1. Automatic route requires prior approval from the RBI for all investments
  2. Government route allows investors to invest without any prior permission
  3. Automatic route does not require prior approval from the government or RBI
  4. Automatic route is only applicable to the agriculture sector
Show answer

Answer: Automatic route does not require prior approval from the government or RBI

Under the automatic route, the investor only notifies the RBI after the investment is made, requiring no prior approval.

Question 32easy

With reference to agricultural reforms, the concept of 'Contract Farming' is intended to achieve which of the following?

  1. Giving the government total control over the pricing of all crops
  2. Reducing the dependence of farmers on private buyers
  3. Linking farmers directly with buyers for pre-determined prices and quality standards
  4. Eliminating the use of technology in traditional farming
Show answer

Answer: Linking farmers directly with buyers for pre-determined prices and quality standards

Contract farming aims to reduce price risk for farmers by fixing prices with buyers before the sowing season.

Question 33easy

If the Reserve Bank of India increases the 'Cash Reserve Ratio' (CRR) as a monetary reform tool, what is the likely immediate impact?

  1. Commercial banks will have more loanable funds
  2. The money multiplier in the economy will increase
  3. The liquidity available with banks for lending will decrease
  4. Interest rates in the economy will automatically fall
Show answer

Answer: The liquidity available with banks for lending will decrease

A higher CRR forces banks to keep more cash with the RBI, reducing the funds available for lending.

Question 34easy

In the context of trade reforms, what does the 'Current Account Deficit' (CAD) specifically represent?

  1. The difference between total foreign assets and total foreign liabilities
  2. When the value of imports of goods and services exceeds the value of exports
  3. The amount of money the government borrows from the World Bank
  4. The total amount of FDI flowing into the country
Show answer

Answer: When the value of imports of goods and services exceeds the value of exports

CAD occurs when the sum of the trade balance and net income/transfers is negative.

Question 35easy

The shift from 'Fixed Exchange Rate' to 'Market-Determined Exchange Rate' in the 1990s was primarily intended to:

  1. Increase the cost of imports to discourage consumption
  2. Improve the balance of payments by making exports more competitive
  3. Prevent any fluctuation in the value of the Rupee
  4. Eliminate the need for foreign exchange reserves
Show answer

Answer: Improve the balance of payments by making exports more competitive

Market-determined rates allow the currency to depreciate if needed, making exports cheaper and more competitive globally.

Question 36easy

With reference to the New Economic Policy of 1991, which of the following best describes the primary objective of 'Liberalization'?

  1. Increasing the state's control over the industrial licensing system
  2. Reducing government regulations and restrictions on private sector entry
  3. Ensuring a fixed exchange rate for the Indian Rupee against the US Dollar
  4. Nationalizing key infrastructure sectors to ensure social equity
Show answer

Answer: Reducing government regulations and restrictions on private sector entry

Liberalization aimed to remove the 'License Raj' and reduce bureaucratic hurdles to encourage private investment.

Question 37easy

In the context of India's fiscal reforms, what is the primary intended effect of implementing a 'Fiscal Responsibility and Budget Management' (FRBM) framework?

  1. To maximize the current account deficit for rapid industrial growth
  2. To eliminate the need for monetary policy interventions by the RBI
  3. To institutionalize financial discipline and limit the government's fiscal deficit
  4. To shift the entire tax burden from direct taxes to indirect taxes
Show answer

Answer: To institutionalize financial discipline and limit the government's fiscal deficit

The FRBM Act seeks to ensure long-term macro-economic stability by limiting government borrowing and reducing the fiscal deficit.

Question 38easy

Which of the following is a likely outcome of 'Sterilized Intervention' by the Reserve Bank of India during a period of heavy capital inflows?

  1. An increase in the domestic money supply to stimulate consumption
  2. The prevention of excessive appreciation of the domestic currency without increasing inflation
  3. A deliberate increase in the fiscal deficit to balance the trade account
  4. The complete abandonment of the managed float exchange rate regime
Show answer

Answer: The prevention of excessive appreciation of the domestic currency without increasing inflation

Sterilization involves offsetting the increase in money supply from forex purchases by selling government securities.

Question 39easy

Consider the impact of the 'Goods and Services Tax' (GST) reform. Which of the following is a core conceptual advantage of this reform over the previous tax regime?

  1. It allows states to independently set varying tax rates for the same product
  2. It eliminates the cascading effect of taxes through a seamless input tax credit
  3. It increases the total number of taxes a manufacturer must comply with
  4. It shifts the entire tax burden from the consumer to the producer
Show answer

Answer: It eliminates the cascading effect of taxes through a seamless input tax credit

GST removes the 'tax on tax' effect by allowing credits for taxes paid on inputs.

Question 40easy

Regarding agricultural reforms in India, what is the conceptual goal of shifting from 'Price Support' (MSP) to 'Income Support' (like PM-KISAN)?

  1. To encourage the overproduction of water-intensive crops like paddy
  2. To reduce market distortions and discourage monoculture while providing a safety net
  3. To eliminate the role of the Food Corporation of India (FCI) entirely
  4. To increase the dependence of farmers on middlemen for credit
Show answer

Answer: To reduce market distortions and discourage monoculture while providing a safety net

Income support provides direct cash transfers, reducing the distortionary effect of price-based incentives.

Question 41easy

If the Reserve Bank of India decides to increase the 'Cash Reserve Ratio' (CRR), what is the most immediate impact on the banking system?

  1. Banks have more loanable funds, leading to lower interest rates
  2. The liquidity in the banking system decreases, potentially raising lending rates
  3. The government's fiscal deficit increases due to lower tax collections
  4. The current account deficit narrows due to increased imports
Show answer

Answer: The liquidity in the banking system decreases, potentially raising lending rates

Higher CRR forces banks to keep more cash with the RBI, reducing the funds available for lending.

Question 42easy

In the context of trade reforms, what does the transition from 'Import Substitution' to 'Export Promotion' signify?

  1. A shift toward protecting domestic industries through high tariffs
  2. A strategy to integrate the domestic economy into global value chains
  3. A move to ban all foreign direct investment in the manufacturing sector
  4. An effort to reduce the total volume of international trade
Show answer

Answer: A strategy to integrate the domestic economy into global value chains

Export promotion focuses on competitiveness and global market integration rather than isolating the domestic market.

Question 43easy

How does a depreciation of the Indian Rupee typically affect India's Balance of Payments (BoP) in the long run, assuming the Marshall-Lerner condition holds?

  1. It makes imports cheaper, leading to a wider trade deficit
  2. It makes exports more competitive, potentially improving the trade balance
  3. It leads to an immediate decrease in the foreign exchange reserves
  4. It eliminates the need for any foreign direct investment
Show answer

Answer: It makes exports more competitive, potentially improving the trade balance

Depreciation makes domestic goods cheaper for foreigners, increasing exports and improving the trade balance.

Question 44easy

Which of the following best describes the concept of 'Financial Inclusion' as a reform goal in the Indian economy?

  1. Restricting banking services to urban centers to ensure stability
  2. Ensuring access to formal financial services for the unbanked and underbanked population
  3. Increasing the interest rates on savings accounts to discourage consumption
  4. Privatizing all public sector banks to improve efficiency
Show answer

Answer: Ensuring access to formal financial services for the unbanked and underbanked population

Financial inclusion aims to bring marginalized sections into the formal banking fold for credit and savings.

Question 45easy

What is the primary objective of the 'Insolvency and Bankruptcy Code' (IBC) reform?

  1. To provide permanent bailouts to failing large corporations
  2. To create a time-bound process for resolving insolvency and recovering stressed assets
  3. To prevent any company from declaring bankruptcy in India
  4. To nationalize all private companies that fail to meet profit targets
Show answer

Answer: To create a time-bound process for resolving insolvency and recovering stressed assets

The IBC provides a legal framework for the efficient resolution of bad loans and exit of failed firms.

Question 46easy

With reference to the 'Sterilization' process adopted by the Reserve Bank of India, which of the following statements is correct?

  1. It is used to neutralize the effect of foreign capital inflows on the domestic money supply.
  2. It involves increasing the Cash Reserve Ratio to encourage commercial lending.
  3. It is a tool used exclusively to combat deflationary pressures in the economy.
  4. It refers to the process of removing bad loans from the balance sheets of public sector banks.
Show answer

Answer: It is used to neutralize the effect of foreign capital inflows on the domestic money supply.

Sterilization involves offsetting the increase in domestic liquidity caused by foreign exchange inflows by selling government securities.

Question 47easy

In the context of India's Balance of Payments, which of the following would lead to a decrease in the Current Account deficit?

  1. An increase in the import of crude oil due to rising global demand.
  2. A significant depreciation of the Indian Rupee against the US Dollar.
  3. An increase in the remittance inflows from Non-Resident Indians.
  4. Both B and C
Show answer

Answer: Both B and C

Rupee depreciation makes exports cheaper and imports costlier, while higher remittances increase credits in the current account.

Question 48easy

Which of the following best describes the 'Twin Deficit' problem in the context of an economy?

  1. Simultaneous occurrence of a high fiscal deficit and a high current account deficit.
  2. Concurrent increase in both inflation and unemployment rates.
  3. A situation where both revenue deficit and capital deficit are increasing.
  4. The gap between the nominal GDP and real GDP combined with a trade deficit.
Show answer

Answer: Simultaneous occurrence of a high fiscal deficit and a high current account deficit.

Twin deficits refer to the simultaneous presence of a large government budget deficit and a large current account deficit.

Question 49easy

If the Reserve Bank of India decides to adopt an 'Accommodative Stance' in its monetary policy, what is the most likely outcome?

  1. An increase in the Repo Rate to curb inflation.
  2. A decrease in the Statutory Liquidity Ratio to restrict credit flow.
  3. Lowering of policy rates to stimulate investment and consumption.
  4. Selling government securities in the open market to mop up liquidity.
Show answer

Answer: Lowering of policy rates to stimulate investment and consumption.

An accommodative stance means the RBI is willing to lower interest rates to support economic growth.

Question 50easy

Consider the following statements regarding 'Capital Account Convertibility' in India. Which of the following is true?

  1. India has full convertibility on both the current and capital accounts.
  2. The current account is fully convertible, while the capital account is only partially convertible.
  3. The capital account is fully convertible to attract Foreign Direct Investment.
  4. Both accounts are partially convertible to maintain exchange rate stability.
Show answer

Answer: The current account is fully convertible, while the capital account is only partially convertible.

India allows full convertibility for trade in goods and services (current account) but regulates capital flows (capital account).

Question 51easy

Which of the following is a primary objective of the 'Insolvency and Bankruptcy Code (IBC)' introduced as a structural reform?

  1. To provide a time-bound process for resolving insolvency of companies and individuals.
  2. To nationalize stressed assets of private banks to prevent systemic collapse.
  3. To eliminate the need for judicial intervention in debt recovery.
  4. To provide direct subsidies to bankrupt firms to maintain employment.
Show answer

Answer: To provide a time-bound process for resolving insolvency of companies and individuals.

The IBC aims to provide a streamlined, time-bound process for resolving insolvency and maximizing the value of assets.

Question 52easy

What is the primary conceptual difference between 'Fiscal Deficit' and 'Primary Deficit'?

  1. Fiscal deficit excludes subsidies, while primary deficit includes them.
  2. Primary deficit is the fiscal deficit minus interest payments on previous borrowings.
  3. Fiscal deficit only considers revenue expenditure, while primary deficit considers capital expenditure.
  4. Primary deficit is always higher than the fiscal deficit in a developing economy.
Show answer

Answer: Primary deficit is the fiscal deficit minus interest payments on previous borrowings.

Primary deficit indicates the government's borrowing requirements excluding the burden of past interest payments.

Question 53easy

Which of the following measures is most likely to be used by the RBI to control 'Cost-Push Inflation'?

  1. Increasing the Repo Rate to reduce aggregate demand.
  2. Implementing supply-side measures such as releasing buffer stocks of food grains.
  3. Decreasing the Cash Reserve Ratio to increase liquidity in the market.
  4. Increasing the government spending on infrastructure projects.
Show answer

Answer: Implementing supply-side measures such as releasing buffer stocks of food grains.

Cost-push inflation is caused by supply shocks; therefore, supply-side interventions are more effective than demand-side monetary tools.

Question 54easy

Which of the following is a characteristic of 'Automatic Stabilizers' in a fiscal policy framework?

  1. Specific legislative acts passed by Parliament to stimulate the economy during a recession.
  2. Tax systems and unemployment benefits that naturally offset fluctuations in economic activity.
  3. Direct interventions by the Central Bank to manage the exchange rate.
  4. The process of adjusting the Repo rate based on the inflation target.
Show answer

Answer: Tax systems and unemployment benefits that naturally offset fluctuations in economic activity.

Automatic stabilizers, like progressive taxes, reduce spending during booms and increase it during recessions without new legislation.

Question 55easy

In the context of agricultural reforms, 'Contract Farming' is primarily intended to achieve which of the following?

  1. Eliminating the role of private players in the procurement of crops.
  2. Reducing the dependence of farmers on the Minimum Support Price (MSP).
  3. Integrating farmers with the value chain by providing price certainty and technology.
  4. Converting all agricultural land into industrial zones for economic growth.
Show answer

Answer: Integrating farmers with the value chain by providing price certainty and technology.

Contract farming links farmers directly to buyers, reducing risk and providing access to better inputs and markets.

Question 56easy

In the context of India's 1991 economic reforms, which of the following was the primary objective of the 'Liberalization' phase?

  1. Increasing the share of public sector in strategic industries
  2. Reducing government control over industrial licensing and permits
  3. Eliminating the current account deficit through import bans
  4. Implementing a fixed exchange rate regime to stabilize the rupee
Show answer

Answer: Reducing government control over industrial licensing and permits

Liberalization aimed to remove the 'License Raj' to encourage private sector growth and industrial efficiency.

Question 57easy

Which of the following best describes the impact of 'Sterilized Intervention' by the Reserve Bank of India (RBI) during periods of high foreign capital inflows?

  1. It prevents the appreciation of the domestic currency without affecting money supply
  2. It offsets the increase in domestic liquidity caused by buying foreign currency
  3. It ensures that the exchange rate remains fixed regardless of market demand
  4. It increases the inflation rate by injecting liquidity into the banking system
Show answer

Answer: It offsets the increase in domestic liquidity caused by buying foreign currency

Sterilization involves selling government securities to mop up the excess liquidity created by buying foreign forex.

Question 58easy

  1. Indian exports become more expensive in the global market
  2. The cost of importing essential commodities like crude oil decreases
  3. The competitiveness of Indian goods in international markets generally increases
  4. Foreign portfolio investors are more likely to increase their holdings in Indian bonds

Answer: The competitiveness of Indian goods in international markets generally increases

A weaker rupee makes Indian exports cheaper for foreign buyers, thereby boosting export competitiveness.

Question 59easy

With reference to the Goods and Services Tax (GST) reform in India, which of the following statements is correct regarding its nature?

  1. It is a direct tax that replaces all corporate taxes
  2. It is a destination-based consumption tax
  3. It allows states to independently set tax rates for all goods
  4. It is an origin-based tax that eliminates the cascading effect
Show answer

Answer: It is a destination-based consumption tax

GST is a destination-based tax, meaning the tax accrues to the state where the goods or services are consumed.

  4. Increase in the velocity of money in the economy

Higher CRR forces banks to keep more cash with RBI, reducing the funds available for lending and lowering liquidity.

  4. The decrease in tax revenue due to an increase in tax exemptions

Fiscal drag occurs when inflation increases nominal income, pushing taxpayers into higher brackets, which acts as a brake on demand.

Question 71easy

Show answer

Answer: It eliminates the tax on previous value additions through the Input Tax Credit mechanism

GST removes the cascading effect by allowing producers to claim credit for taxes paid on inputs.

Question 112easy

  2. Devaluation occurs in a fixed exchange rate regime, while depreciation occurs in a floating regime
  3. Devaluation increases the value of the currency, while depreciation decreases it

Show answer

Answer: Devaluation occurs in a fixed exchange rate regime, while depreciation occurs in a floating regime

  4. Increase in the value of foreign portfolio investments flowing into the equity market
Show answer

Answer: Increase in the cost of imports and a potential improvement in the trade balance

Depreciation makes exports cheaper and imports costlier, which can theoretically improve the trade balance via the J-curve effect.

Question 115easy

In the context of fiscal reforms, what does 'Fiscal Drag' typically refer to in an economy?

  1. A situation where inflation pushes taxpayers into higher tax brackets, reducing disposable income
  2. The delay in the implementation of budget allocations by various government ministries
  3. The increase in public debt resulting from high revenue deficits
  4. The reduction in government spending during a period of economic boom
Show answer

Answer: A situation where inflation pushes taxpayers into higher tax brackets, reducing disposable income

Fiscal drag occurs when inflation increases nominal income, moving taxpayers into higher brackets and acting as an automatic stabilizer.

Question 116easy

Regarding the 'Open Market Operations' (OMO) conducted by the RBI, which action would be taken to curb inflationary pressures in the economy?

  1. Purchase of government securities from the open market
  2. Sale of government securities to commercial banks
  3. Reduction in the Repo Rate to encourage borrowing
  4. Lowering the Marginal Standing Facility (MSF) rate
Show answer

Answer: Sale of government securities to commercial banks

Selling securities absorbs liquidity from the banking system, reducing the money supply and curbing inflation.

Automatic stabilizers like progressive taxes and welfare payments dampen economic fluctuations without requiring new legislation.

The MPC targets Consumer Price Index (CPI) inflation at 4% within a band of 2% to 6%.

Question 119easy

  3. To shift the entire tax burden from indirect taxes to direct taxes

Answer: To eliminate the cascading effect of taxes by creating a seamless chain of input tax credits

GST removes the 'tax on tax' effect, ensuring that tax is levied only on the value added at each stage.

Question 122easy

  3. Capital account records only FDI, while Current account records only FPI

Show answer

Answer: Current account records trade in goods, services, and transfers; Capital account records financial assets and liabilities

The Current Account tracks the flow of goods/services/income, while the Capital Account tracks the change in ownership of national assets.

Question 128easy

What is the conceptual difference between 'Devaluation' and 'Depreciation' of the currency?

  3. Devaluation increases the value of the currency, while depreciation decreases it
  4. There is no conceptual difference; both terms are used interchangeably
Show answer

Answer: Devaluation occurs in a fixed exchange rate system, while depreciation occurs in a floating system

Devaluation is a deliberate downward adjustment by the authority; depreciation is a market-driven decline in value.

Question 162medium

Question 163medium

  3. Fiscal deficit has no impact on the interest rates of the private sector.
  4. Crowding out occurs when the government reduces spending to lower the fiscal deficit.
Show answer

Answer: High fiscal deficit leads to higher government borrowing, increasing interest rates and reducing private investment.

Crowding out occurs when heavy government borrowing raises interest rates, making it expensive for the private sector to borrow.

  2. Stressed balance sheets of both banks and corporates
  3. Deficit in both Current Account and Fiscal Account
  4. Excess liquidity in banks and low demand from consumers
Show answer

Answer: Stressed balance sheets of both banks and corporates

It refers to the simultaneous stress of NPAs in banks and over-leveraged corporate balance sheets.

Question 171medium

  4. Neither 1 nor 2

Question 172medium

  2. The cost of servicing external debt increases
  3. Exports become less competitive in global markets

Question 174medium

Question 184medium

In the context of Monetary Policy, if the Reserve Bank of India (RBI) decides to engage in 'Sterilized Intervention' to manage the exchange rate, what is the primary objective?

  3. To intentionally depreciate the rupee to boost trade
  4. To increase the statutory liquidity ratio for commercial banks

Answer: To neutralize the effect of foreign exchange inflows on domestic liquidity

Sterilization prevents excess liquidity from foreign exchange purchases from causing inflation by selling government securities.

Question 188medium

Question 189medium

  2. Selling government securities to absorb excess liquidity

Selling securities removes liquidity from the banking system, reducing the money supply and curbing inflation.

Question 196medium

Question 198medium

FDI is a capital flow and is therefore recorded in the Capital Account, not the Current Account.

Question 199medium

  4. Neither 1 nor 2
Show answer

Answer: Both 1 and 2

The base effect occurs when the comparison point (previous year) is unusually low or high, distorting the percentage change.

Question 200medium

  2. High Fiscal Deficit and High Current Account Deficit
  3. High Revenue Deficit and High Primary Deficit
  4. Low GDP growth and Low Foreign Exchange Reserves
Show answer

Answer: High Fiscal Deficit and High Current Account Deficit

Twin deficits occur when a country runs both a budget deficit (fiscal) and a trade deficit (current account).

Question 206medium

Question 208medium

The J-curve shows that trade balance worsens initially due to fixed contracts before improving as volumes adjust.

Question 228medium

Show answer

Answer: It makes exports cheaper and imports costlier, potentially improving the trade balance.

Depreciation makes domestic goods cheaper for foreigners (boosting exports) and foreign goods costlier for locals (curbing imports).

Question 248medium

  3. It leads to an immediate decrease in the current account deficit without any lag

Question 289medium

Which of the following measures would be most effective for the RBI to curb 'Cost-Push Inflation' in the Indian economy?

  1. Increasing the Cash Reserve Ratio (CRR) to reduce money supply
  2. Implementing supply-side reforms to reduce raw material costs
  3. Increasing the Repo Rate to dampen aggregate demand
  4. Reducing the Statutory Liquidity Ratio (SLR) to encourage lending
Show answer

Answer: Implementing supply-side reforms to reduce raw material costs

Cost-push inflation is caused by supply shocks; monetary tightening (Repo/CRR) addresses demand-pull inflation, not supply costs.

Question 290medium

Regarding the 'Capital Account Convertibility' in India, which of the following statements is correct?

  1. India has full convertibility on both the Current Account and Capital Account.
  2. India has full convertibility on the Capital Account but partial on the Current Account.
  3. India has full convertibility on the Current Account but partial on the Capital Account.
  4. India maintains a strict regime of non-convertibility for both accounts.
Show answer

Answer: India has full convertibility on the Current Account but partial on the Capital Account.

India allows free conversion for trade/services (Current Account) but regulates capital flows (Capital Account) via FEMA.

Question 292medium

  2. Cash Reserve Ratio and Statutory Liquidity Ratio
  3. Marginal Standing Facility and Bank Rate
  4. Open Market Operations and Moral Suasion
Show answer

Answer: Repo Rate and Reverse Repo Rate

LAF allows banks to manage liquidity through Repo (borrowing) and Reverse Repo (depositing) with the RBI.

Stagflation is a rare combination of stagnant economic growth, high unemployment, and high inflation.

Question 301medium

The 'Base Effect' in the context of inflation calculation refers to:

  2. The weightage given to food items in the CPI basket.
  3. The difference between WPI and CPI indices.
  4. The impact of global commodity prices on domestic inflation.
Show answer

Answer: The impact of the previous year's price levels on the current inflation rate.

The base effect occurs when a low price in the base period makes the current percentage increase appear higher.

Question 336medium

Question 342medium

Show answer

Question 375medium

The RBI's policy rate is 6.5%. If inflation expectations rise to 5% while actual CPI is 4%, the real policy rate is:

  1. 2.5%
  2. 1.5%
  3. 3.5%
  4. 6.5%
Show answer

Answer: 2.5%

Real rate = nominal rate – expected inflation = 6.5% – 4% = 2.5% (using CPI) or 6.5% – 5% = 1.5% (expectations); the question asks for real policy rate using CPI, hence 2.5%.

Answer: Integrating farmers with the value chain and reducing price volatility

Contract farming links farmers directly with buyers to ensure price certainty and quality standards.

Question 403medium

Regarding the 'Goods and Services Tax (GST)' reforms in India, which of the following statements is correct regarding its impact on the 'Cascading Effect'?

  1. It increased the tax burden by adding taxes on top of taxes.
  2. It eliminated the tax on value addition at each stage by allowing Input Tax Credit.
  3. It shifted the entire tax burden to the final consumer without any credit mechanism.
  4. It replaced only the direct taxes to ensure a seamless flow of credits.
Show answer

Answer: It eliminated the tax on value addition at each stage by allowing Input Tax Credit.

GST removes the cascading effect by allowing producers to claim credit for taxes paid on inputs.

Question 406medium

Depreciation makes Indian goods cheaper for foreigners (boosting exports) and foreign goods costlier (reducing imports).

Question 436medium

Question 450medium

Both rising raw material costs (oil) and rising labor costs (wages) increase production costs, pushing prices upward.

Regarding the impact of Rupee depreciation on India's Balance of Payments, which of the following is most likely to occur?

  1. Immediate improvement in the current account deficit due to increased export competitiveness
  2. Decrease in the cost of importing crude oil and gold
  3. Decrease in the external debt burden denominated in foreign currency
  4. Automatic reduction in the Trade Deficit without considering the elasticity of demand
Show answer

Answer: Immediate improvement in the current account deficit due to increased export competitiveness

Depreciation makes exports cheaper and imports costlier, potentially improving the trade balance if the Marshall-Lerner condition holds.

Question 466medium

Which of the following best describes the 'Impossible Trinity' (Trilemma) in international economics?

  4. Foreign Direct Investment, Portfolio Investment, and External Commercial Borrowings

Answer: Fixed exchange rate, Free capital movement, and Independent monetary policy

A country cannot simultaneously maintain a fixed exchange rate, free capital flow, and an independent monetary policy.

Question 489medium

  3. OMO increases the money supply, while QE always decreases it

Question 493hard

If the Indian government decides to shift from a 'Fiscal Deficit' target to a 'Primary Deficit' target for its budgetary goals, what would be the primary conceptual implication?

Question 494hard

Question 512hard

In the context of India's Balance of Payments (BoP), if the country experiences a persistent current account deficit funded by a surplus in the capital account, what is the most likely long-term structural risk?

Question 513hard

Which of the following best describes the 'Impossible Trinity' (Mundell-Fleming Trilemma) as it applies to India's monetary policy framework?

  1. India cannot simultaneously maintain a fixed exchange rate, free capital movement, and an independent monetary policy.
  2. India cannot maintain high growth, low inflation, and low fiscal deficit simultaneously.
  3. India cannot have a current account surplus, capital account surplus, and stable exchange rates.
  4. India cannot maintain a gold standard, floating exchange rate, and independent interest rates.
Show answer

Answer: India cannot simultaneously maintain a fixed exchange rate, free capital movement, and an independent monetary policy.

The Trilemma states a country can only choose two of the three: fixed exchange rate, free capital flow, and independent monetary policy.

Question 514hard

Regarding the shift from 'Minimum Support Price' (MSP) to 'Price Deficiency Payment' (PDP) in agricultural reforms, what is the primary conceptual objective?

PDP pays the difference between MSP and market price directly to farmers without requiring physical procurement.

  1. Decrease in the government's interest payment burden.
  2. Increase in the cost of borrowing for the government due to higher interest payments on sterilized bonds.
  3. Immediate reduction in the fiscal deficit due to increased forex reserves.
  4. No impact on the fiscal position as sterilization is a purely monetary tool.
Show answer

Answer: Increase in the cost of borrowing for the government due to higher interest payments on sterilized bonds.

Selling bonds to sterilize inflows creates a liability for the RBI/Government, increasing interest payment costs.

Answer: To provide a legal framework for price and quality agreements between farmers and buyers.

Contract farming provides a legal framework for pre-harvest agreements on price and quality, reducing market risk for farmers.

  1. The lack of land ownership among marginal farmers by providing them with land titles.
  2. The volatility of farm-gate prices and the lack of access to high-quality inputs and markets.
  3. The over-reliance on monsoon rains by mandating the construction of drip irrigation systems.
  4. The inefficiency of the MSP system by replacing all government procurement with private contracts.
Show answer

Answer: The volatility of farm-gate prices and the lack of access to high-quality inputs and markets.

Contract farming reduces price risk for farmers and provides guaranteed markets and technical inputs through private partnerships.

Question 615hard

Which of the following statements regarding the 'Current Account' and 'Capital Account' of the Balance of Payments (BoP) is correct?

  1. A surplus in the Current Account must always be offset by a surplus in the Capital Account.
  2. Unilateral transfers, such as remittances, are recorded in the Capital Account.
  3. A deficit in the Current Account is financed by a surplus in the Capital Account (borrowings or investments).
  4. The Capital Account only records the trade of physical goods and services.
Show answer

Answer: A deficit in the Current Account is financed by a surplus in the Capital Account (borrowings or investments).

In BoP accounting, a current account deficit must be balanced by a surplus in the capital account (net inflow of capital).

Question 617hard

In the context of India's transition towards a 'Market-Linked' exchange rate regime, how does a significant depreciation of the Rupee typically impact the Current Account Deficit (CAD)?

  2. It may initially widen the CAD due to the 'J-curve effect' before improving it in the long run.
  3. It has no impact on CAD as the trade balance is determined solely by global demand.
  4. It leads to a permanent reduction in CAD by eliminating the need for foreign exchange reserves.
Show answer

Answer: It may initially widen the CAD due to the 'J-curve effect' before improving it in the long run.

The J-curve effect suggests CAD worsens initially as import costs rise before export volumes adjust.

Higher rates dampen demand, whereas infrastructure spending can raise demand and costs, leading to uncertain net effect.

Question 663hard

Under the 'Agricultural Debt Waiver Scheme', a large number of farmers obtain debt relief. Which of the following is a likely unintended macro‑economic consequence?

  1. Moral hazard leading to higher future credit demand from the agricultural sector.
  2. Immediate reduction in fiscal deficit due to lower debt servicing costs.
  3. Strengthening of the banking sector’s balance sheets through reduced NPAs.
  4. Appreciation of the rupee as agricultural output spikes.
Show answer

Answer: Moral hazard leading to higher future credit demand from the agricultural sector.

Debt waivers can encourage future borrowing, creating moral hazard and higher credit demand.
